We need to find the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. It's stated that the correct answer is A, 0.04 V, but I need to understand why.

First, electromagnetic induction. Faraday's Law, right? The induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt), where N is the number of turns, and Φ is the magnetic flux.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the area. In this case, the field is perpendicular, so cosθ is 1, so Φ = B * A.

Alright, so let's compute ΔΦ first. Initially, B is 0.01 T, and the area is 0.2 m², so initial flux Φ₁ = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

Finally, B is 0.06 T, so Φ₂ = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ = Φ₂ - Φ₁ = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So the rate of change of flux is ΔΦ/Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s.

But wait, that's the rate of change. Since the magnetic field is increasing, the flux is also increasing, so the induced EMF should be positive, right? But actually, the negative sign in Faraday's Law depends on the direction of the induced current, which we don't need to compute here since we're only asked for the average magnitude. So the magnitude is N * ΔΦ/Δt.

ε = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where:
- ε is the induced EMF,
- N is the number of turns in the coil,
- ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux,
- Δt is the time over which the change occurs.

So, first, let me figure out the change in magnetic flux (ΔΦ). The magnetic flux Φ is given by:

Φ = B * A * cosθ

But in this problem, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, so the angle θ between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil is 0 degrees. Therefore, cosθ is 1, and Φ simplifies to:

Φ = B * A

So, the initial magnetic flux Φ₁ is:

Φ₁ = B₁ * A = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m²

And the final magnetic flux Φ₂ is:

Φ₂ = B₂ * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m²

Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ is:

ΔΦ = Φ₂ - Φ₁ = 0.012 T·m² - 0.002 T·m² = 0.01 T·m²

Okay, so the change in flux is 0.01 T·m². Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. Plugging these into Faraday's Law:

ε = -N * (ΔΦ / Δt) = -250 * (0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s)

Let me compute that. First, 0.01 divided by 0.25. Hmm, 0.01 / 0.25 is the same as 0.01 * (1 / 0.25) = 0.01 * 4 = 0.04. So:

ε = -250 * 0.04 T·m²/s

Multiplying 250 by 0.04 gives:

250 * 0.04 = 10

--------------------------------------------------
Okay, so I've got this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction, and I need to figure out why the answer is 0.04 V. Let me read it again.

"A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 s, the average induced EMF in the coil is... The options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. Why the correct answer is: A. 0.04 V?"

Alright, so the question is about the average induced EMF in a coil when the magnetic field changes. I remember that Faraday's Law of Induction is involved here. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil.

So, first, let me recall the formula for magnetic flux. Magnetic flux, Φ, is given by the product of the magnetic field (B), the area (A) it's passing through, and the cosine of the angle between them. Since the magnetic field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, the angle is 0 degrees, so cos(0) is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

In this case, the initial magnetic field is 0.01 T, and it increases to 0.06 T. The area of the coil is 0.2 m², and the coil has 250 turns. Wait, so does the number of turns affect the flux? Hmm, actually, I think the number of turns affects the total magnetic flux linkage, not the flux itself. So, the flux through one turn is B*A, and with 250 turns, the total flux linkage is Φ_total = N * Φ_one_turn = N * B * A. So that's where the 250 comes in.

But when we're calculating the induced EMF, I think we need the change in magnetic flux, which is the change in the total flux linkage. So, the change in B is from 0.01 T to 0.06 T, so ΔB is 0.06 - 0.01 = 0.05 T. --------------------------------------------------
Alright, so I've got this physics problem here, and I'm trying to figure it out step by step. Let me read it again:

"A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 s, the average induced EMF in the coil is... The options are: A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. Why the correct answer is: A. 0.04 V?"

Okay, so the question is about electromagnetic induction, specifically the induced EMF in a coil when the magnetic field changes. I remember Faraday's Law of Induction is involved here. Let me recall what that says. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * dΦ/dt

Where:
- EMF is the induced electromotive force,
- N is the number of turns in the coil,
- Φ is the magnetic flux,
- dΦ/dt is the rate at which flux is changing.

So, let's break this down. First, I need to find the magnetic flux Φ. Magnetic flux is given by the product of the magnetic field B, the area A of the coil, and the cosine of the angle θ between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil's plane. In this case, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane, so θ is 0 degrees, and cos(0) is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

The initial magnetic field is 0.01 T, and it increases to 0.06 T. So, the change in B, ΔB, is 0.06 - 0.01 = 0.05 T. The area A is given as 0.2 m². Therefore, the change in magnetic flux ΔΦ is ΔB * A = 0.05 T * 0.2 m² = 0.01 Wb (webers).

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So, the rate of change of flux dΦ/dt is ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 Wb / 0.25 s = 0.04 Wb/s.

Next, the number of turns N is 250. Plugging these into Faraday's Law:

Okay, so I have this question about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to work through it step by step. 

First, the problem says there's a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of this coil. So, the coil is in a magnetic field, and the field is increasing over time. The question is about finding the average induced EMF in the coil.

The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 seconds. They give four options for the average induced EMF: A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. And they mention the correct answer is A, 0.04 V. Hmm, let me see why that is.

I remember Faraday's Law of Induction, which states that the induced EMF in a coil is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * dΦ/dt

Where N is the number of turns in the coil, and Φ is the magnetic flux. 

So, first, I need to calculate the magnetic flux Φ before and after the change, and then find the rate of change, dΦ/dt.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area of the coil, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil's plane. In this case, the field is perpendicular, so θ is 0 degrees, and cosθ is 1. So, Φ = B * A.

Given that, initial flux Φ_initial = B_initial * A = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

Similarly, the final flux Φ_final = B_final * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

So, the change in flux, ΔΦ, is Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Then, the induced EMF is given by EMF = -N * dΦ/dt. Since the question is about the average induced EMF, the negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but we're only concerned with the magnitude here, so we can ignore the sign.

So, EMF = N * |dΦ/dt| = 250 turns * 0.04 T·m²/s = 10 V.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to figure it out step by step. First, let me read the question again to make sure I understand it.

"A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 s, the average induced EMF in the coil is... The options are: A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is A. 0.04 V. Why?"

Alright, so I need to find the average induced EMF in the coil due to the change in magnetic field over time. I remember Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction, which states that the induced EMF is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula for that is:

\( \mathcal{E} = -N \frac{\Delta \Phi_B}{\Delta t} \)

Where \( \mathcal{E} \) is the induced EMF, \( N \) is the number of turns in the coil, \( \Delta \Phi_B \) is the change in magnetic flux, and \( \Delta t \) is the time interval over which the change occurs.

First, let's break down what each term means.

Magnetic flux \( \Phi_B \) is given by the product of the magnetic field \( B \), the area \( A \) through which the field passes, and the cosine of the angle \( \theta \) between the magnetic field and the normal to the area. Since the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, the angle \( \theta \) is 0°, and the cosine of 0° is 1. So, the flux is just \( B \times A \).

Given that, the initial magnetic flux \( \Phi_{B_i} \) is:

\( \Phi_{B_i} = B_i \times A = 0.01 \, T \times 0.2 \, m² = 0.002 \, Wb \) (Webbens, the unit for magnetic flux).

Similarly, the final magnetic flux \( \Phi_{B_f} \) is:

\( \Phi_{B_f} = B_f \times A = 0.06 \, T \times 0.2 \, m² = 0.012 \, Wb \).

So, the change in magnetic flux \( \Delta \Phi_B \) is:

\( \Delta \Phi_B = \Phi_{B_f} - \Phi_{B_i} = 0.012 \, Wb - 0.002 \, Wb = 0.01 \, Wb \).

Now, the time interval \( \Delta t \) is given as 0.25 seconds.

Putting it all into Faraday's Law:

\( \mathcal{E} = -N \frac{\Delta \Phi_B}{\Delta t} \)

We have \( N = 250 \) turns, \( \Delta \Phi_B = 0.01 \, Wb \), and \( \Delta t = 0.25 \, s \).

Calculating the induced EMF:

\( \mathcal{E} = -250 \times \frac{0.01}{0.25} \)

Let me compute that step by step:

First, divide \( 0.01 \) by \( 0.25 \):

\( \frac{0.01}{0.25} = 0.04 \)

Then, multiply by 250:

\( 250 \times 0.04 = 10 \)

--------------------------------------------------
Okay, so I've got this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction, and I need to figure out why the average induced EMF is 0.04 V. Let me go through it step by step.

First, the problem says there's a magnetic field directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil. The coil has an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. We need to find the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options given are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is A, 0.04 V. Hmm, let me see why.

Alright, I remember Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction. It states that the induced EMF in a coil is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns in the coil, and Φ is the magnetic flux.

So, magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. Since the field is perpendicular, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

Alright, so initially, the magnetic field B₁ is 0.01 T, and the area A is 0.2 m². So initial flux Φ₁ = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

Then, the magnetic field increases to B₂ = 0.06 T. So the final flux Φ₂ = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

The change in flux ΔΦ is Φ₂ - Φ₁ = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 / 0.25 = 0.04 T·m²/s.

Since EMF is -N * dΦ/dt, the negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but since we're only asked about the magnitude of the average induced EMF, we can ignore the negative sign.

So, EMF = N * |dΦ/dt| = 250 * 0.04 = 10 V. Wait, that's 10 volts. But the correct answer is 0.04 V. Hmm, that doesn't add up. Did I make a mistake somewhere?

First, the question says there's a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil. Initially, the magnetic field is 0.01 T, and it's increased to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. They're asking for the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is A, 0.04 V. So, I need to understand why.

Okay, I remember from my physics class that when the magnetic field through a coil changes, it induces an electromotive force (EMF) in the coil. This is due to Faraday's Law of Induction. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil.

The formula for magnetic flux is Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil. In this case, the magnetic field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, so θ is 0 degrees, and cosθ is 1. So, the flux simplifies to Φ = B * A.

But in this problem, the field is changing over time, so we need to consider the change in flux. The average induced EMF (ε) is given by Faraday's Law as:

ε = -ΔΦ/Δt

But since they're asking for the average induced EMF, the negative sign indicates the direction, but the magnitude is what's important here. So, we can disregard the negative sign and just take the absolute value.

So, let me write that down.

First, find the change in magnetic flux (ΔΦ). The initial flux is Φ_initial = B_initial * A. The final flux is Φ_final = B_final * A. So, ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = (B_final - B_initial) * A.

Now, plugging in the numbers:

B_initial = 0.01 T
B_final = 0.06 T
A = 0.2 m²
Δt = 0.25 s

So, ΔΦ = (0.06 - 0.01) * 0.2 = (0.05 T) * 0.2 m² = 0.01 Wb (weber is the unit for magnetic flux).

Wait, hold on. The induced EMF is the change in flux over time, right? So, ε = ΔΦ / Δt.

So, ε = 0.01 Wb / 0.25 s = 0.04 V.

Ah, okay, so that's where the 0.04 V comes from. But wait, I almost forgot the number of turns. The coil has 250 turns. How does that factor into this?

Oh, right! When a coil has multiple turns, each turn contributes to the total induced EMF. So, the induced EMF is not just from a single turn but from all the turns. Therefore, the total induced EMF would be 250 times the EMF induced by one turn.

Wait, so does that mean we need to multiply the single-turn EMF by the number of turns?

Let me think. Each individual turn will have an EMF induced due to the change in flux through that turn. So, if there are 250 turns, each with the same change in flux, the total EMF would be 250 times the single-turn EMF.

So, actually, I think I missed the number of turns in my initial calculation.

But since there are 250 turns, the total induced EMF would be 250 * 0.04 V = 10 V.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Hmm, let me read it again and see if I can figure it out step by step.

The question says: A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 s, the average induced EMF in the coil is... and then there are four options: A is 0.04 V, B is 0.1 V, C is 2.5 V, D is 10 V. The correct answer is given as A, 0.04 V, but I need to understand why.

Alright, so first, I remember that when the magnetic field through a coil changes, it induces an electromotive force (EMF) in the coil. This is Faraday's Law of Induction. The formula for the average induced EMF is usually given by:

\[ \text{EMF} = -N \cdot \frac{\Delta B}{\Delta t} \cdot A \]

where:
- \( N \) is the number of turns in the coil,
- \( \Delta B \) is the change in magnetic field,
- \( \Delta t \) is the time over which the change occurs,
- \( A \) is the area of the coil.

Wait, but in this formula, the negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current according to the right-hand rule, but since the question is asking for the average EMF, the magnitude is what matters, so maybe the negative sign isn't important here. I can just calculate the magnitude.

So, let's break down the given values:

- Area \( A = 0.2 \, \text{m}^2 \)
- Number of turns \( N = 250 \)
- Initial magnetic field \( B_{\text{initial}} = 0.01 \, \text{T} \)
- Final magnetic field \( B_{\text{final}} = 0.06 \, \text{T} \)
- Time interval \( \Delta t = 0.25 \, \text{s} \)

First, let's compute the change in magnetic field \( \Delta B \):

\[ \Delta B = B_{\text{final}} - B_{\text{initial}} = 0.06 \, \text{T} - 0.01 \, \text{T} = 0.05 \, \text{T} \]

Okay, so the magnetic field increases by 0.05 Tesla over 0.25 seconds.

Now, plug these values into the formula:

\[ \text{EMF} = N \cdot \frac{\Delta B}{\Delta t} \cdot A \]

Plugging in the numbers:

\[ \text{EMF} = 250 \cdot \frac{0.05}{0.25} \cdot 0.2 \]

Let me calculate each part step by step.

First, compute \( \frac{0.05}{0.25} \):

0.05 divided by 0.25. Hmm, 0.25 goes into 0.05 how many times? Well, 0.25 times 0.2 is 0.05, because 0.25 * 0.2 = 0.05. So, \( \frac{0.05}{0.25} = 0.2 \).

So now, the formula simplifies to:

\[ \text{EMF} = 250 \cdot 0.2 \cdot 0.2 \]

Faraday's Law: EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where Φ is the magnetic flux.

Magnetic flux Φ = B * A * cos(theta), and since the field is perpendicular, theta is 0, so cos(theta) is 1.

Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, change in flux ΔΦ = ΔB * A.

Thus, EMF = -N * ΔΦ / Δt = -N * (ΔB * A) / Δt.

So, the magnitude is N * (ΔB * A) / Δt.

So, that's the same as N * ΔB / Δt * A.

So, same as my previous calculation.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Hmm, let me see what it's asking. There's a circular coil with an area of 0.2 square meters and 250 turns. The magnetic field is initially 0.01 Tesla and then it increases to 0.06 Tesla over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. They want to know the average induced EMF in the coil. The options given are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is supposed to be A, 0.04 V. Hmm, okay, let's break this down step by step.

First, I remember Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction, which deals with induced EMF in a coil when there's a change in magnetic flux. The formula for the induced EMF is ε = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns, and Φ is the magnetic flux. The negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but since they're only asking for the magnitude, I can ignore the sign.

So, let's identify the values. The area of the coil is 0.2 m², which is the same as the magnetic flux for one turn. The number of turns is 250. The magnetic field changes from 0.01 T to 0.06 T. So, the initial magnetic field B_initial is 0.01 T, and the final magnetic field B_final is 0.06 T. The time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds.

Now, magnetic flux Φ is calculated as Φ = B * A * cosθ, where θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil. Since the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, the change in magnetic flux, ΔΦ, would be Φ_final - Φ_initial. Let's compute that:

ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = (B_final * A) - (B_initial * A) = (0.06 T * 0.2 m²) - (0.01 T * 0.2 m²) = (0.012 - 0.002) T·m² = 0.01 T·m².

So, the total change in flux is 0.01 Weber (since 1 Weber = 1 T·m²). 

Next, we need to find the rate of change of flux with time, which is dΦ/dt. Since ΔΦ = 0.01 Wb over Δt = 0.25 s, the average rate is:

dΦ/dt = ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 / 0.25 = 0.04 Wb/s.

So, the induced EMF is N multiplied by this rate:

ε = N * (dΦ/dt) = 250 * 0.04 Wb/s = 10 Wb/s.

Wait, 10 Wb/s? Hmm, that's 10 volts, right? Because 1 Weber is equal to 1 volt-second. So, 10 Wb/s is 10 volts. But the options are given, and one of them is 10 V, which is option D. But the correct answer is supposed to be A, 0.04 V. So, something's not right here.

"A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. Why the correct answer is: A. 0.04 V?"

Alright, so we have a coil with 250 turns, area 0.2 m², and the magnetic field is increasing from 0.01 T to 0.06 T over 0.25 seconds. They want the average induced EMF.

Hmm, okay, so I remember that Faraday's Law of Induction is used for this. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns, and Φ is the magnetic flux.

But wait, since they are asking for the average induced EMF, I think we don't need to worry about the negative sign because it just indicates the direction of the induced current, but the magnitude is what's important here.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by B * A * cos(theta), where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and theta is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. In this case, the field is perpendicular to the plane, so theta is 0 degrees, cos(theta) is 1. So Φ = B * A.

So, the change in flux ΔΦ is the final flux minus the initial flux: ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = (B_final * A) - (B_initial * A).

Calculating that, ΔΦ = (0.06 T * 0.2 m²) - (0.01 T * 0.2 m²) = (0.012 - 0.002) T·m² = 0.01 T·m².

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So, the rate of change dΦ/dt is ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s.

Then, the induced EMF is N * dΦ/dt. The number of turns N is 250, so EMF = 250 * 0.04 T·m²/s = 10 V. Wait, that's 10 volts, which is option D. But the correct answer is supposed to be A, 0.04 V.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to figure it out step by step. The question says:

"A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 s, the average induced EMF in the coil is... The options are: A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. Why the correct answer is: A. 0.04 V?"

Hmm, so I need to find the average induced EMF in the coil. I remember Faraday's Law of Induction is involved here. Let me recall Faraday's Law.

Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF in a coil is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * dΦ/dt

Where:
- N is the number of turns in the coil.
- Φ is the magnetic flux.
- t is the time.

Since the question asks for the average induced EMF, I can ignore the negative sign because it just indicates the direction of the induced current, which isn't required here.

First, I need to calculate the change in magnetic flux, ΔΦ. Magnetic flux is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil's plane. In this problem, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane, so θ = 0 degrees, and cos(0) = 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, initially, the magnetic field is B_initial = 0.01 T, and the area A = 0.2 m². Thus, initial flux Φ_initial = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

Finally, the magnetic field increases to B_final = 0.06 T. So, the final flux Φ_final = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.010 T·m².

Now, the change in time Δt is given as 0.25 s.

So, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is ΔΦ / Δt = 0.010 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s.

Now, applying Faraday's Law, EMF = -N * dΦ/dt. Since the number of turns N is 250, plug that in:

EMF = -250 * 0.04 = -10 V. But the question asks for the average induced EMF, and the negative sign is just about the direction, not the magnitude. So the magnitude is 10 V. Wait, but the options don't have 10 V as the correct answer? Wait, hold on, the options do have D. 10 V. But the given correct answer is A. 0.04 V. That doesn't match.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to work through it step by step. Maybe if I break it down, it'll make more sense.

The problem says: A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. If the magnetic field is increased from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 seconds, the average induced EMF in the coil is... and then there are four options.

First, I remember that Faraday's Law of Induction is involved here. Faraday's Law relates the induced electromotive force (EMF) in a coil to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * dΦ/dt

Where:
- N is the number of turns in the coil,
- Φ is the magnetic flux,
- t is the time interval.

Since the question is asking for the average induced EMF, I can ignore the negative sign because it just indicates the direction of the induced current, which isn't asked here.

So, let's identify the values given:
- Area, A = 0.2 m²,
- Number of turns, N = 250,
- Initial magnetic field, B_i = 0.01 T,
- Final magnetic field, B_f = 0.06 T,
- Time interval, Δt = 0.25 s.

I need to find the change in magnetic flux, ΔΦ, over the time interval. Magnetic flux is given by the product of the magnetic field and the area through which it passes, multiplied by the cosine of the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. Since the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, the angle θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, the initial flux, Φ_i = B_i * A = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

The final flux, Φ_f = B_f * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Therefore, the change in flux, ΔΦ = Φ_f - Φ_i = 0.012 T·m² - 0.002 T·m² = 0.01 T·m².

Now, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is ΔΦ divided by Δt. So:

dΦ/dt = ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s.

Then, the EMF is equal to the negative of N times dΦ/dt. But since we're only interested in the magnitude, we can ignore the negative sign:

EMF ≈ N * |dΦ/dt| = 250 * 0.04 T·m²/s = 10 V.

ΔΦ = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Δt = 0.25 s.

Thus, dΦ/dt = 0.01 / 0.25 = 0.04 T·m²/s.

I remember that Faraday's Law of Induction is involved when there's a change in magnetic flux through a coil, which induces an electromotive force, or EMF, in the coil. The question is about finding the average induced EMF in a circular coil when the magnetic field changes over a certain time interval.

First, let me parse the problem:

- We have a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m².
- The coil has 250 turns.
- The magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil.
- The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds.
- We need to find the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are given as A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V.
- The correct answer is stated as A. 0.04 V.

Hmm, okay. So, I need to recall Faraday's Law. From what I remember, Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. Mathematically, it's written as:

ε = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where ε is the induced EMF, N is the number of turns in the coil, ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux, and Δt is the time over which the change occurs.

Alright, so I need to compute ΔΦ first. Magnetic flux Φ is given by the product of the magnetic field B, the area A through which it passes, and the cosine of the angle θ between the magnetic field and the normal to the area. Since the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, the angle θ is 0 degrees, so cos(0) is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, the initial magnetic flux Φ₁ is B₁ * A, and the final flux Φ₂ is B₂ * A. Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ is Φ₂ - Φ₁ = (B₂ - B₁) * A.

Plugging in the numbers:

B₁ = 0.01 T, B₂ = 0.06 T, A = 0.2 m².

ΔΦ = (0.06 - 0.01) * 0.2 = 0.05 * 0.2 = 0.01 Wb. (Wb is Weber, the unit for magnetic flux.)

Now, the time interval Δt is given as 0.25 seconds. So, ΔΦ/Δt is 0.01 Wb / 0.25 s = 0.04 Wb/s.

But wait, Faraday's Law has a negative sign, but since the question is asking for the average induced EMF, and it's just asking for the magnitude, I think we can ignore the negative sign for now because it just indicates the direction of the induced current, which isn't required here.

So, the average induced EMF ε is equal to N multiplied by ΔΦ/Δt.

N is 250 turns.

So, ε = 250 * 0.04 = 10 V.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to figure it out step by step. Sometimes I get confused with these concepts, so I need to take it slow.

The question says: There's a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of this coil. Initially, the magnetic field is 0.01 T, and it's increased to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. The question is asking for the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is given as A. 0.04 V, so I need to understand why.

Alright, let's start by recalling Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF in a coil is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where:
- N is the number of turns in the coil.
- ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux.
- Δt is the time over which the change occurs.

So, to find the EMF, I need to compute the change in magnetic flux over the change in time and then multiply it by the number of turns.

First, what is magnetic flux? Magnetic flux Φ is given by:

Φ = B * A * cosθ

Where:
- B is the magnetic field.
- A is the area through which the field passes.
- θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface.

In this problem, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil. That means the angle θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, the initial magnetic flux Φ_initial is:

Φ_initial = B_initial * A = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m²

Similarly, the final magnetic flux Φ_final is:

Φ_final = B_final * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m²

Now, let's compute the change in flux ΔΦ:

ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 T·m² - 0.002 T·m² = 0.01 T·m²

Okay, so the change in flux is 0.01 T·m². Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds.

So, the rate of change of flux is ΔΦ/Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s

Now, applying Faraday's Law, the induced EMF is:

EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt) = -250 * 0.04 T·m²/s = -10 V

Alright, the problem says: A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil of area 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 seconds. We need to find the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is said to be A. 0.04 V.

Hmm, okay. So let me recall Faraday's Law of Induction. As I remember, Faraday's Law states that the induced electromotive force (EMF) in a coil is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * ΔΦ/Δt

Where N is the number of turns in the coil, and ΔΦ/Δt is the rate of change of magnetic flux.

Alright, so in this problem, the magnetic field is changing, which affects the magnetic flux. The magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. Since the field is directed perpendicular to the plane, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, initially, when B is 0.01 T, the flux is Φ₁ = 0.01 T * 0.2 m². Let me calculate that: 0.01 * 0.2 = 0.002 Weber (since Weber is the unit for magnetic flux).

Then, when the magnetic field increases to 0.06 T, the flux becomes Φ₂ = 0.06 T * 0.2 m². That's 0.06 * 0.2 = 0.012 Weber.

So the change in flux ΔΦ is Φ₂ - Φ₁ = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 Weber.

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So ΔΦ/Δt is 0.01 Wb / 0.25 s = 0.04 Wb/s. So the rate of change of flux is 0.04 Wb/s.

But wait, let me double-check that calculation: 0.01 divided by 0.25 is indeed 0.04? Hmm, 0.25 goes into 0.01 how many times? Well, 0.25 times 0.04 is 0.01, yes, that's correct.

First, let me recall Faraday's Law. It says that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The magnetic flux, Φ, is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil. Since the field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. That simplifies things.

So, the induced EMF, ε, is equal to the change in magnetic flux over time, ΔΦ/Δt. In formula terms: ε = -ΔΦ/Δt. The negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but since the question is only asking for the magnitude of the average EMF, we can ignore the sign.

Let me compute the change in magnetic flux first. The initial magnetic field, B_initial, is 0.01 T, and the final, B_final, is 0.06 T. The area is given as 0.2 m².

Final flux, Φ_final = B_final * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Therefore, the change in flux, ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Now, the time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds. So, the average induced EMF is ε_avg = ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s.

Calculating that: 0.01 divided by 0.25 is 0.04. So, ε_avg = 0.04 V.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to figure it out step by step. The question is about finding the average induced EMF in a circular coil when the magnetic field changes over a certain time interval. 

Alright, the problem states: A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil. The coil has an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 seconds. The options for the average induced EMF are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is said to be A, 0.04 V. Let me try to see why that is.

First, I remember that Faraday's Law of Induction is the main concept here. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF in a coil is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where:
- N is the number of turns in the coil,
- Φ is the magnetic flux,
- ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux,
- Δt is the time interval over which the change happens.

So, let's identify the values given in the problem:
- Area of the coil, A = 0.2 m²
- Number of turns, N = 250
- Initial magnetic field, B_initial = 0.01 T
- Final magnetic field, B_final = 0.06 T
- Time interval, Δt = 0.25 s

First, I need to calculate the change in magnetic flux, ΔΦ. Magnetic flux is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil's plane. In this case, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane, so θ = 0°, and cos(0°) = 1. So, Φ = B * A.

Therefore, the initial flux Φ_initial = B_initial * A = 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m².

Similarly, the final flux Φ_final = B_final * A = 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Change in flux ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 T·m² - 0.002 T·m² = 0.01 T·m².

Now, using Faraday's Law, the average induced EMF is:

EMF_avg = -N * (ΔΦ / Δt)

But since the problem is asking for the magnitude of the EMF, we can ignore the negative sign. So,

EMF_avg = N * (ΔΦ / Δt) = 250 * (0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s)

Let me compute that:

First, divide ΔΦ by Δt: 0.01 / 0.25 = 0.04 T

Then multiply by N: 250 * 0.04 = 10 V

Wait, that gives me 10 V, which is option D, but the correct answer is supposed to be A, 0.04 V. Hmm, I must have done something wrong here.

Wait a second, let me double-check my calculations. Maybe I messed up the units or the formula.

So, the formula is EMF = N * (ΔΦ / Δt). Let me write that again:

EMF = N * ( (B_final * A - B_initial * A) / Δt )

Plugging in the numbers:

Compute the numerator inside the brackets first:

0.06 * 0.2 = 0.012

0.01 * 0.2 = 0.002

So, 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01

Then, 0.01 / 0.25 = 0.04

Then, EMF = 250 * 0.04 = 10 V

The question says: A magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T during a time interval of 0.25 seconds. Okay, so first, Faraday's Law of Induction states that the induced EMF is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil, right? Mathematically, it's EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns, and Φ is the magnetic flux. The negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but since we're only asked about the magnitude, maybe I can ignore the sign for now.

So, magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. In this problem, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, so θ is 0 degrees. Cos(0) is 1, so Φ = B * A.

Let me plug in the numbers. The area A is 0.2 m², and the magnetic field changes from 0.01 T to 0.06 T. So, the initial flux Φ_initial is 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m². The final flux Φ_final is 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

The change in flux ΔΦ is Φ_final - Φ_initial, so that's 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m². The time interval Δt is 0.25 seconds.

So, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is ΔΦ / Δt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s. But wait, that's the rate of change, and EMF is the negative of N times that. So, EMF = -N * dΦ/dt.

The number of turns N is 250. So, EMF = -250 * 0.04 T·m²/s = -10 V. The negative sign tells me the direction is opposite to the increasing magnetic field, but since we're asked for the average induced EMF, we take the magnitude, so the EMF is 10 V.

The formula for induced EMF is ε = N * (ΔΦ/Δt), where N is the number of turns in the coil, ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux, and Δt is the time over which the change happens. So, I need to compute ΔΦ first.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the surface. Since the field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ is 1. That simplifies things because Φ = B * A.

So, initially, the magnetic field is 0.01 T, and the area is 0.2 m². So, Φ_initial is 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m². Then, after the change, the magnetic field becomes 0.06 T, so Φ_final is 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m².

Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ is Φ_final - Φ_initial = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m².

Alright, so I've got this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction, and I need to figure out why the correct answer is 0.04 volts. Hmm, let's go through it step by step.

First, the question says there's a circular coil with an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field is initially 0.01 T and then increases to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. They want the average induced EMF in the coil. The options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is A, 0.04 V. I need to understand why.

Okay, so I remember Faraday's Law of Induction. It states that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns and Φ is the magnetic flux.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cos(theta), where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and theta is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the area. Since the field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, theta is 0 degrees, so cos(theta) is 1. So, Φ = B * A.

Let me write that down:

Φ = B * A

So, the change in magnetic flux ΔΦ is:

ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = (B_final * A) - (B_initial * A)

That's equal to (B_final - B_initial) * A.

So, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is:

dΦ/dt = (B_final - B_initial) * A / Δt

Then, plug that into Faraday's Law:

EMF = -N * (B_final - B_initial) * A / Δt

Since EMF is a magnitude, the negative sign just indicates the direction, which we can ignore here.

So, EMF = N * (B_final - B_initial) * A / Δt

Alright, let's plug in the numbers.

N = 250 turns

B_initial = 0.01 T

B_final = 0.06 T

A = 0.2 m²

Δt = 0.25 s

0.06 T - 0.01 T = 0.05 T

So, the change in magnetic field is 0.05 T.

Now, plug that into EMF:

EMF = 250 * 0.05 T * 0.2 m² / 0.25 s

First, I remember that when the magnetic field through a coil changes, it induces an electromotive force (EMF) in the coil. The formula for the induced EMF is given by Faraday's Law of Induction. The formula is EMF = N * ε * B Δt, where N is the number of turns, ε is the induced electromotive force per turn, B is the change in magnetic field, and Δt is the time interval over which the change occurs.

In this case, the magnetic field is perpendicular, so θ is 0 degrees, and cosθ is 1. So, Φ = B * A.

Therefore, the change in flux ΔΦ would be ΔB * A. So, substituting back into the EMF formula, EMF = N * (ΔB * A) / Δt. That makes sense.

Let me write this down:

EMF = N * (ΔB * A) / Δt

EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where N is the number of turns in the coil, ΔΦ is the change in magnetic flux, and Δt is the time over which the change occurs. The negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, which is important for the physical understanding but not necessary for calculating the magnitude of the EMF.

Okay, so let's break this down. The coil has 250 turns, so N = 250.

In this case, the magnetic field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, so θ = 0 degrees, and cosθ = 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about electromagnetic induction. Let me try to figure it out step by step. The question says that there's a magnetic field directed perpendicular to the plane of a circular coil. The coil has an area of 0.2 m² and 250 turns. The magnetic field increases from 0.01 T to 0.06 T over a time interval of 0.25 seconds. I need to find the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A. 0.04 V, B. 0.1 V, C. 2.5 V, D. 10 V. The correct answer is supposed to be A. 0.04 V, but I want to understand why.

First, I remember Faraday's Law of electromagnetic induction. It states that the induced EMF is equal to the rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula for that is EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns and Φ is the magnetic flux. The negative sign indicates the direction of the induced current, but since the question only asks for the magnitude, I can ignore the sign for now.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where B is the magnetic field, A is the area, and θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil's plane. In this case, the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane, so θ is 0 degrees. Cos(0) is 1, so Φ = B * A.

Let me note down the given values:
- Area, A = 0.2 m²
- Number of turns, N = 250
- Initial magnetic field, B_initial = 0.01 T
- Final magnetic field, B_final = 0.06 T
- Time interval, Δt = 0.25 s

So, first, I need to find the change in magnetic flux, ΔΦ. Since Φ = B * A, the change in flux is ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial = (B_final * A) - (B_initial * A).

Calculating Φ_final: 0.06 T * 0.2 m² = 0.012 T·m²
Calculating Φ_initial: 0.01 T * 0.2 m² = 0.002 T·m²
So, ΔΦ = 0.012 - 0.002 = 0.01 T·m²

Next, I need to find the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt. That would be ΔΦ divided by Δt. So:

dΦ/dt = 0.01 T·m² / 0.25 s = 0.04 T·m²/s

Now, applying Faraday's Law, the induced EMF is:

EMF = N * |dΦ/dt| = 250 * 0.04 T·m²/s = 10 V

In this problem, it says the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the plane of the coil, so theta is 0 degrees. Cos(0) is 1, so Φ = B * A.

Wait, let me just verify the formula once again.

Faraday's Law: EMF = -N * dΦ/dt.

Φ = B * A * cos(theta).

So, EMF = -N * d(B*A)/dt.

Which is -N * (dB/dt * A + B * dA/dt). But in this problem, the area A is constant, and B is changing, so it's -N * A * dB/dt.

Hence, EMF = -N * A * (dB/dt).

The negative sign indicates the direction, but the magnitude is N * A * (dB/dt).

So, plugging in the numbers: N=250, A=0.2, dB/dt=(0.06 - 0.

First, I recall Faraday's Law of Induction. It says that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. Mathematically, it's EMF = -N * dΦ/dt, where N is the number of turns and Φ is the magnetic flux.

Let me write down the given values:

- Area of the coil (A) = 0.2 m²
- Number of turns (N) = 250
- Initial magnetic field (B_initial) = 0.01 T
- Final magnetic field (B_final) = 0.06 T
- Time interval (Δt) = 0.25 s

I need to find the change in magnetic flux (ΔΦ) over time (Δt) because that will give me dΦ/dt, which I can multiply by N to get EMF.

Magnetic flux Φ is given by Φ = B * A * cosθ, where θ is the angle between the magnetic field and the normal to the coil. Since the magnetic field is directed perpendicular to the coil's plane, θ is 0 degrees, so cosθ = 1. Therefore, Φ = B * A.

So, the initial flux Φ_initial is B_initial * A, and the final flux Φ_final is B_final * A. The change in flux ΔΦ is Φ_final - Φ_initial.

Calculating ΔΦ:

ΔΦ = Φ_final - Φ_initial
ΔΦ = (B_final * A) - (B_initial * A)
ΔΦ = A * (B_final - B_initial)

So, plugging in the numbers:

ΔΦ = 0.2 m² * (0.06 T - 0.01 T)
ΔΦ = 0.2 m² * 0.05 T
ΔΦ = 0.01 Wb (Webers)

Now, the rate of change of flux, dΦ/dt, is ΔΦ / Δt.

So, dΦ/dt = 0.01 Wb / 0.25 s

EMF = -N * dΦ/dt

The question is asking for the average induced EMF in the coil, and the options are A through D, with the correct answer being A, 0.04 V.

Hmm, okay. So, I think I need to use Faraday's Law here. Faraday's Law states that the induced EMF is equal to the negative rate of change of magnetic flux through the coil. The formula is:

EMF = -N * (ΔΦ/Δt)

Where N is the number of turns, and ΔΦ/Δt is the change in magnetic flux per unit time. Since the magnetic field is perpendicular to the plane of the coil, the magnetic flux Φ through each turn is given by Φ = B * A, where B is the magnetic field and A is the area.

So, let's compute ΔΦ first. The initial magnetic flux Φ_initial is B_initial * A. The final flux Φ_final is B_final * A. The change in flux ΔΦ is Φ_final - Φ_initial.

Plugging in the numbers: B_initial is 0.01 T, B_final is 0.06 T, and A is 0.2 m².

ΔΦ = (0.06 T * 0.2 m²) - (0.01 T * 0.2 m²)
ΔΦ = (0.012 T·m²) - (0.002 T·m²)
ΔΦ = 0.01 T·m²

Wait, 0.06 times 0.2 is 0.012, and 0.01 times 0.2 is 0.002. Subtracting gives 0.01 T·m². Okay, that makes sense.

Calculating that: 0.01 divided by 0.25 is 0.04 T·m²/s.
